guide About the project Why we flagged this facility Harm Home cited for three or more violations that harmed a resident or placed them at high risk of harm. Includes injuries, elopements, neglect, exploitation and physical or verbal abuse. Widespread deficiencies Home cited for violations across at least four categories. This facility had a change in name, owner or operator during its inspection history. If violations were recorded before that change, they are factored into this flag. More Personal Care Home Sandy Springs-Memory Care / Sandy Springs Personal Care 1260 and 1262 Hightower Trail, Sandy Springs, GA 30350 License: PCH008812 / PCH008813 Beds: 109/56 website Contact the AJC about this facility .To navigate, press the arrow keys.Keyboard shortcutsMap DataMap data ©2022 GoogleTerms of UseReport a map errorMap data ©2022 GoogleThis page can't load Google Maps correctly.Do you own this website?OK Facility response Read this facility's response to our request for comments How does this home compare to others? Each facility analyzed by the AJC has been inspected by the Georgia Department of Community Health. Most have received citations for problems in the past four years. What to look for The blue bars show the distribution of violations of standards for all assisted living communities and large personal care homes, beginning in 2015. The total number of violations during that period is divided by the number of annual, initial and other routine inspections to give every home a consistent base for comparison. The dashed line shows where this home falls in that distribution, and the number above the arrow indicates its violation ratio. If the dashed line falls further to the right, this home had more violations. Violations per routine inspection(Lower numbers are better)Number of homes0102030020406080This home7.2 Inspection reportsPolice reportsFood inspections Georgia’s Department of Community Health conducts routine inspections of assisted living communities and personal care homes and cites homes for deficiencies. Complaints by residents or their families and a facility’s self-reported incidents can also prompt an inspection. The AJC compiled inspections associated with each facility from 2015-2019, including current and prior operators at the same address. This senior care community has more than one licensed facility at the same location. We have noted the license types on this page and have combined the inspection information to show the community’s complete record. The AJC determined three types of severity indicators based on our analysis of inspection violations: Harm: includes harm to one or more residents or a serious violation capable of causing harm. Higher severity: includes violation of unusually serious nature. Medium severity: includes violation of serious but less severe nature. Previous citation: includes violation for which home was cited at one prior inspection. Previous citation: includes violation for which home was cited at two prior inspections. Previous citation: Previous citation: includes violation for which home was cited at three or more prior inspections. DateTypeViolations 10/2/19 routine - Hide details No rule violations were cited as a result of this inspection. 8/7/19 complaint 1 Hide details Statute Inspection record text (appears as recorded in state records) Supporting Residents' Rights 111-8-62-.25(1)(a) Based on record review and interview, the facility failed to ensure each resident received care and services which were adequate, appropriate and in compliance with applicable federal and state law and regulations for 1 of 3 residents (Resident #1). Findings include: A review of the file for Resident #1, admitted 8/28/18, diagnoses of hypertension, limited walking and Cerebrovascular Accident. A review of an incident report dated 6/29/19 showed that Resident #1 had an unwitnessed fall. Further review of the report showed that the family was not notified of the fall. During an interview on 7/23/19, FF stated the facility did not notified the family of the fall on 6/29/19. FF further stated that the family knew of the resident's fall when they were at the facility visiting the next day. During an interview at 2:45 p.m., Resident #1 stated he/she had a fall a month ago and fractured his/her left shoulder. During an interview on 8/1/19 at 10:00 a.m., Staff A stated the family of Resident #1 was not notified of the 6/29/19 fall. During an interview on 7/2/19 at 7:29 a.m., Staff C stated that he/she came to work on 6/6/19 at approximately 10:46 p.m. and counted the medication for Resident #1, discovered the missing Fentanyl 75 mcg patches and reported the incident to Staff D. AA also stated that on 6/3/19 the facility took possession of five (5) Fentanyl 75 mcg patches but he/she was not present during the transfer. AA stated that on 6/5/19, three (3) additional patches were located in lost luggage and given to the staff at the facility. AA stated he/she took a photograph of Staff A administering a patch for Resident #1. During an interview at 10:30 a.m. Staff E stated that on 6/6/19 he/she worked 7:00 a.m. to 8:00 p.m. counted the medication before leaving and didn't see any narcotic inventory sheet for Resident #1 or the Fentanyl 75 mcg patches. Facility's Fax Order dated 4/21/17 at 10:25 p.m. to Resident #1's physician, showed, "Resident #1 had "a swollen knee and was having a lot of pain and discomfort." 4). Physician's Fax Order dated 4/23/17 at 11:16 a.m., showed that Staff K sent a request to Resident #1's physician that documented, Resident #1 was still complaining of pain in Left leg, and that an x-ray from his/her hip to knee was requested. 5). Further review of the note, showed that BB asked Staff K if he/she knew what had caused Resident #1 to be in pain and that Staff K had stated that he/she did not know, and that Resident #1 had received an x-ray of his/her Left foot on 4/21/17, with negative result, and that another order for an x-ray of Resident #1's Left hip and knee was requested. 6). During an interview on 8/23/16 at 4:00 p.m., Staff A stated that Resident #3 had agreed to relocate to a vacant room until the repair was made to his/her air conditioner.
